Misthological Models Part 6                                                                                 Page 168
a more robust model for interpreting the prayer soteriologically on behalf of believers or reconsider whether the
prayer is intended to be understood as a soteriological request on behalf of believers.

        Presumptive Conditionality

                                                         1Jn 3:2
          Jesus’ unstated presumption of conditionality underlies various aspects of His prayer. Beasley-Murray’s
comment on Jn 17:20 reveals a couple of such assumptions: “That Jesus should pray for those ‘who are to believe
through their word’ assumes the success of the disciples’ mission (alluded to in v 18) and the reality of their
consecration to the task (v 19)” (WBC). The contingent faithfulness and fruitfulness of the Eleven is the presumed
premise for this request. As to Jn 17:24, Beasley-Murray notes: “The thought of the prayer is remarkably similar to
that in 1 John 3:2.” True, but in that context, unfaithful believers shrink away from the Lord in shame (1Jn 2:18).
Beasley-Murray quotes both of these epistolary cross references and rightly says, “The parallel is instructive for our
passage.” The parallel that he focuses upon is the timing, so that both passages are dealing with eschatological
glorification. However, the parallel also indicates the misthological nature of that glorification. This glory is not
given freely to all believers.
          As I deduced and explained at length in RBVGB, when Christ appears and believers are transformed into
immortal bodies, many of these transformed believers will be put to shame. “When He appears” (1Jn 2:28; 3:2),
they will all see Him, but some will fail to become like Him (1Jn 3:2) and thus be put away in shame from before
Him (1Jn 2:28; cp. Ps 1:5; Mk 8:38; Lk 9:26; Jude 1:24). The imagery of this truth is most vivid in Rev 3:18, where
transformed believers are ashamed of their misthological nakedness because they are walking about in the raw—
completely devoid of white garments, just as Jesus anticipated (Mt 22:12). These unfaithful believers do not shine
at all. Therefore, their bodies would be described as immortal and imperishable but not glorious.
          Beasley-Murray goes on to say regarding the parallel between Jn 17:24 and 1Jn 3:2, “The ‘beholding’ of
the glory of Jesus will result in the participation by his people in that glory.” Beasley-Murray speaks the truth, but
not the whole truth. As I also pointed out in RBVGB, all believers will see Jesus and be transformed into His
likeness in some capacity or another. But Jesus can be seen in a mere resurrected body, as He was on the road to
Emmaus (Lk 24:13-31), or in a glorified body (Rev 1:12-17), which invokes such a sense of awe that mortals fall
down as if dead before it. As noted in MMP3, everyone will stand before God in judgment at some point
(Rev 20:15), but only misthologically worthy believers will be able to stand it (Lk 21:36; cp. 1Jn 2:28). Overcomers
have the strength to stand (CT) and are counted worthy of standing (MT). They will be transformed into the same
type of glorious body as the Lord and thus be able to stand before the Lord’s glorious body. Accordingly, in
conjunction with the deductions being made here in MMP6, we can now postulate a spatial clarification that will
easily reconcile the puzzle between the parallels.
          In 1Jn 3:2, John says, “When He appears, we shall be like Him, because we shall see Him just as He is.”
Yet, John presents us with a riddle since, three verses earlier, he also says: “Little children, abide in Him, so that
when He appears, we may have confidence and not shrink away from Him in shame at His coming” (1Jn 2:28).
Why would unfaithful believers shrink away in shame from Jesus if they are going to be like Him? Apparently,
when Jesus appears, not all believers are going to be glorious like Him. All children of God have the potential to be
like Jesus, provided they abide in Him. John had stated the conditional nature of this glorification in v. 28. Three
verses later, John is speaking presumptively when he says we will be like Him. Presuming we abide in Him, we
will be like Him. One might suppose that John is thinking about New Jerusalem, which he describes in Revelation.
After all, only bridal believers will be able to live in New Jerusalem. Unfaithful believers will not even be able to
enter it. I have made such arguments in my earlier writings. But in the present discussion we can press that argument
even further. Even angels, who are the friends of the Bridegroom, can see Jesus in New Jerusalem. Since we
may reasonably suppose that John presumes a parallel in 1Jn 3:2 with his statement in Jn 17:24, we can
deduce that only the Bride can see the Lord in the Where-I-AM bridal chamber, as John indicated in
Jn 12:26; 14:2-3.
          Michaels (NICNT, 17:24) is correct insofar as he goes: “What he wants rather is for his disciples ‘to be
with me where I am,’ something he has already promised them (14:3 and 12:26), and he is not afraid to make his
wants known boldly…. The phrase ‘where I am’ echoes 12:26 and 14:3 verbatim.” As already mentioned, Michaels
takes 12:26 as dealing with a reward. Therefore, if he and other commentators are to be consistent, they should
conclude that Jesus’ request in 17:23 echoes the misthological nature of His promise in 12:26. Brown (AYB) is
Chapter 4. God’s Misthological Temple                                                                           Page 169
correct, therefore, to note the conditional premise for sharing this location: “Eventually those who serve and follow
Jesus will be with him (12:26, 14:3).” In his general comment on the prayer, Brown said, “There can be no doubt
that what he asks for will be granted, for his will and the Father’s will are one.” On the contrary, how can there be
no doubt that His prayer will be answered when He has conditioned its fulfillment on the obedience of the believer?
Simple. Jesus is praying that His prayer will be granted conditionally and no doubt that this is the way it will
be answered. One need not suppose that Jesus is asking the Father to overwrite believers’ free will to grant His
will. He could pray in the confidence of His Father’s ability to answer His prayer without having to resort to
irresistibility. His Father’s ability is not limited to irresistibility.

                                                        2Cor 3:18
          Commentators commonly cite 2Cor 3:18 as a parallel to Jn 17:24 and assume that Paul’s affirmation of
transformative glory applies to all believers since he uses pas: “But we all [pas], with unveiled face beholding as
in a mirror the glory of the Lord, are being transformed into the same image from glory to glory.” In contrast, I did
an analysis distinguishing between the inclusive and exclusive first-person plural in the Corinthian epistles and
determined that about 82% of the time, it is exclusive usage, referring to Paul and his fellow associates, not referring
to the readers (see CC). I perceive 2Cor 3:18 to be in this category also, which is consistent with the determination
that in 2Cor 5:20 Paul and his fellow ministers are urging the Corinthian believers to be reconciled to God via the
we-you contrast. This assessment is also consistent with the analysis done in RBVGB that the transformative glory
of Phil 3:21 is misthological and contingent on attaining the misthological out-resurrection in Phil 3:11.
Contextually, therefore, my argument would be supported by those commentators who perceive an exclusive we
(i.e., an apostolic we) in 2Cor 3:18. For example, Bengel states that it refers to “we all, the ministers of the New
Testament, in antithesis to Moses, who was but one person….The antithesis is hid, 4:3.” In other words, the apostolic
we in the next verse after 2Cor 3:18, which is 1Cor 4:1, “we have this ministry,” clearly refers to the apostles. The
reference to our gospel being veiled from those who are perishing is also an apostolic our. In 2Cor 3:18, the apostles
are experiencing the opposite of a veiled experience regarding the gospel. They are experiencing the unveiled glory
of the Lord and being transformed by it.
          Lange (ACHS) disputes this proposal with an appeal to 2Cor 4:3,6: “(We) includes not merely the Apostle
and his fellow-laborers, or the Apostle and all who preach the Gospel (Catholics appeal to chap. 4:1, and contrast
πάντες [pantes] (all) with the single individual Moses), but all believers, who, the connection shows, must be
included in the πάντες. (Chap 4:3 and 6).” Yet Bengel has the better argument regarding 2Cor 4:3,6, to which Lange
appeals in support. Plummer (ICC) seeks to counter Bengel by claiming that an apostolic we in 2Cor 3:18 would
weaken the antithesis, stating that the “antithesis, contrast is marked by πάντες, which is in antithesis to the one
Moses. But this contrast is greatly weakened if, with Bengel and others, we confine ἡμεῖς, as in vv. 1–12, to ‘we
ministers of the Gospel.’ There is a tone of triumph in πάντες, which would be out of place if the meaning were
confined to a handful of teachers.”
          This argument backfires, though, since Bengel and others who confine the we to the apostolic circle in
2Cor 4:1-12 definitely have the upper hand. Nevertheless, for sake of argument, suppose, as unlikely as it may be,
that the majority opinion is correct and that Paul is referring to all believers. Even in that case, Paul is not referring
to an unconditional transformation, but one that requires beholding the glory of the Lord, a “continuous perception
of Christ,” as even Thrall (ICC), a proponent of the majority position, concedes, acknowledging that continuous
contemplation is required for this progressive glorification. Hunt (GNTC), likewise a proponent of the majority
position, is straightforward with the conditionality: “Paul says that if believers look in God’s Word and see the
beauty of God’s Son, they will be transformed” (bold his.) If, and only if, believers invest their time in God’s word
will they experience this transformation. Of course, the internal logic of such an argument greatly weakens the
notion that it applies to all believers. Either Paul is referring to all believers conditionally, and thus merely
potentially, or just to the apostolic circle in actuality. Belleville (IVPNTC) acknowledges: “We … all might well
be Paul’s way of broadening his point of reference to include all believers. Even so, the focus is still on the new
covenant minister.” The principle applies to all believers even if the interpretation is limited to the apostolic circle.
All believers, who contemplate the Lord’s glory via the word, will be transformed by His word internally in their
spirit so that they can participate in the Lord’s glory misthologically. Many believers fail to meet this condition.
Does this mean that Jesus’ prayer in Jn 17 has failed? No. Jesus was well acquainted with the failures of
believers of His own time and could foresee the failure of future believers. The divisions within the Church
today would be no surprise to Jesus in the Upper Room. He did not intend for His prayer to make such
Misthological Models Part 6                                                                                Page 170
failures impossible for the unfaithful, rather to make victory possible for the faithful. Judged from this
vantage point, His prayer is completely successful. His prayer enables His Bride to clothe Herself with
righteous garments so that She can be with Him in the Bridal City and its Upper Chambers. The full number
of His Bride will be completed.


        Summary
         The Bible presents Earth as God’s footstool (Is 66:1; Mt 5:35; Acts 7:49). In terms of temple typology,
Earth can be pictured as the porch of God’s temple. When Jesus ascended on high, far above all Heavens, He left
the earthly porch, ascended into the skies above Earth, and passed through the created heavens to reach His eternal
abode with the Father in their eternal heaven (Eph 4:10; Heb 4:14). Consequently, He passed through the first,
second, and third heavens to reach the eternal abode of God—the highest heavenly level.
                              Illustration 49. Temple Chambers and Heavenly Cities




Logical inferences lead to the postulation that the Lord’s passing through the heavens to reach the eternal throne of
the Father was accomplished by the Lord using the 3D City as a transport vessel in leading captivity captive (Eph
4:8) from Earth to the 4D City, as discussed in MMP5. As demonstrated in the present study, the Lord left Earth to
prepare a place for His Bride as a new addition to the Father’s house. The Father’s house/temple has various
compartments. The 4D City and 3D City were already in existence when Jesus ascended. The Father’s house is a
two-chambered dwelling best identified with the 4D and 3D City. Therefore, the new addition that Jesus left to add
onto the Father’s house cannot be equated with modifications inside of these preexisting structures. Instead, in
accordance with temple typology, upper room typology, and bridal typology, the exegetical evidence discussed in
the present book confirms the logical inference made in MMP5 that the Bride has a 5D place prepared for Her. This
honeymoon cabin, so to speak, is likely a 5D City. The new place is a new room/city added to the preexisting two
rooms/cities. Just as the two-chambered tabernacle became a three-chambered temple, the Father’s two-chambered
house will become a three-chambered house.
                       Illustration 50. Temple Chambers and Heavenly Cities and Realms
Chapter 4. God’s Misthological Temple                                                                          Page 171
         God is not limited to the realms pictured in this illustration. He has an eternal realm. Through means of the
created realms and structures created within them, He is able to share His habitation with created creatures in lower
realms. God currently dwells visibly in the 4D angelic realm, and in the future, He will dwell visibly in the 3D
human realm (Rev 21:3). The Lord Jesus will visibly elevate the Bride by making the 3D City Her 3D dwelling
place where She can rule 3D creatures and be worshipped by them. Such actions will also be applicable to Her in
the 4D City. However, neither the 3D City nor the 4D City is the new dwelling that He Himself has gone to prepare.
In accordance with the historical bridal background, Jesus affirms that He Himself will prepare this place (Jn 14:2-
3). In that culture, the son, not the servants or hired help, would build a new addition unto his father’s house to serve
as the bridal suit. The father’s approval of the son’s workmanship would determine when the father would tell his
son that his son could now go and claim his bride. The Lord is personally building this structure for us. Angels
cannot prepare this new dwelling for the Bride because angels are 4D beings. They cannot access this new 5D
location. Although new dwellings are undoubtedly being prepared for the Bride inside the 3D City (and thus the
4D City), the new bridal addition unto the Father’s house that Jesus is preparing is best perceived as a 5D addition.
This 5D City will provide private quarters reserved for the Lord and His Bride. Human and angelic friends of the
Bride will not be able to access this intimate realm.


        A Corollary Regarding Jn 14:6
          In TOD, I assumed that Heaven was the Heavenly City and that Jn 14:6 was a soteriological text describing
how to get to Heaven: “Jesus said to him, ‘I am the way, and the truth, and the life; no one comes to the Father, but
through Me’” (Jn 14:6). Thus, I posed the following illustration picturing Jesus Himself as the straight and narrow
way through which one enters Heaven, with the disclaimer that even misthopoligists can allow the soteric
implementation of Heavenly Jerusalem in this illustration if it is acknowledged that all raptured believers freely
enter the City at the time of the rapture. At that time, I thought that expulsion from the City would only become a
misthological issue after the Bema. Therefore, for the sake of simplicity, the City was allowed to represent Heaven
in this illustration in accordance with the working model of the interim state, which I held at the time I wrote TOD.
                                             Illustration 51. Narrow Way




         In TOD, I argued that Jesus was identifying Himself soteriologically as the way to Heaven, as on other
occasions, when with similar metaphors, He said, “Truly, truly, I say to you, I am the door of the sheep…. I am
the door; if anyone enters through Me, he shall be saved” (Jn 10:7-9). I posed that we may likewise understand
Jesus as saying, “I am the straight and narrow way through which one enters Heaven.” As soon as a person enters
this gate, he or she has eternal life (Jn 5:24). I went on to say that a believer does not have to wait until he or she
reaches Heaven to receive eternal life. Believers are assured of reaching Heaven because of their position in Christ,
rather than because of their performance in Christ. They are placed on a conveyor belt from which they cannot fall
and from which they cannot escape that will take them straight to Heaven because they have eternal life. It is a
conveyor belt, not a treadmill, much less an uphill treadmill. As far as their position (security) in Christ and their
entrance into Heaven are concerned, believers passively let the conveyor belt do all the work in taking them to
Heaven. Such was my thinking at that time.
Misthological Models Part 6                                                                                    Page 172
         Several corrections must be made to my earlier position in TOD. This misthological series has shown the
fallacy of equating the Heavenly City with Heaven. The Heavenly City is only a part of Heaven. This misthological
series has also demonstrated that expulsion from the City does not have to await the Bema. Preliminary exclusion
from the City can be experienced by unfaithful believers even before the Bema. Moreover, the proposition that all
raptured believers freely enter the City at the time of the rapture has been replaced with a more refined proposition
that believers are summoned to the Bema stadium atop the Heavenly City at the point of the rapture. Thus, unfaithful
believers never enter the Heavenly City. The new correction now to be noted because of MMP6 is to pose that
Jn 14:6 is probably not a soteric text, or even a dualistic soteric-mistholic text, but an exclusively mistholic text. It
is situated in a context saturated with conditional requirements for those who are already believers.
                                 Illustration 52. Way to the Father and His House




         In Jn 14:6, Jesus is not telling His disciples how to get to His Father’s kingdom; rather, Jesus is telling them
how to get to His Father’s house, even more specifically to the new addition that Jesus will be preparing for His
obedient followers in His Where-I-AM-Place. The way to having this abode with the Father is repeatedly stated in
the context as to abide in Christ by lovingly abiding in His word (Jn 13:17, 34-35; 14:21,23; 15:6,10,14; 16:27),
which makes sense since Jesus is the Word (Jn 1:1). Those believers who do not do so will be cast away and have
no part with Christ in this Prepared Place (Jn 13:8; 15:6). The Prepared Place is only for those believers for whom
it has been prepared, that is, obedient believers. For Jesus to come and receive believers to this place, they must be
in the group for whom it is being prepared (Jn 14:2-3). Therefore, the vastly improved illustration of Jn 14:6 pictures
the way to the Father as walking through (thus abiding in) the word (representing the Word) as one’s means of
qualifying to enter the three compartments of the Father’s house: the 3D City, the 4D City, and ultimately the 5D
City, as typified by the Temple (in relation to the Holy Place, the Holy of Holies, and the Upper Chamber), as Jesus
relates in the Upper Room.
         Commentators frequently point out that Jesus is the way not only to the Father but to the Father’s house
(e.g., WBC). Many assume that the Father’s house is a picture of Heaven and would thereby presume that Jn 14:6
is a picture of saving faith. More astutely, some commentators perceive that something more than a punctiliar
Chapter 4. God’s Misthological Temple                                                                        Page 173
response of faith is entailed. Carson (PNTC), for example, says that Jesus is “the way for his disciples to
attain the many dwelling-places in the Father’s house (vv. 2–3).” Very good. But what do you have to do
to obtain such a dwelling. Carson points out that a statement by Kempis is often quoted: “Follow thou me.
I am the way and the truth and the life….I am the way which thou must follow; the truth which thou
must believe; the life for which thou must hope.” Simply believing is not enough; following Christ is also
entailed. Behavior, not mere belief, is required. Keener (IVPBBC) acknowledges this to be the case from the
OT background: “The ‘way’ in many Jewish texts refers to the righteous way to behave but here possibly
echoes Isaiah’s way back to the new Jerusalem through the wilderness (cf. Jn 1:23).” A moral journey
would thus be envisioned. The imagery is that of a journey to be undertaken, not of a gate to be entered: “‘If we
may so speak, this distance to be traversed’ (Milligan and Moulton). All along the course to the Father’s house
they are still with Him” (Vincent, WSNT). Some would suggest road as a suitable translation (UBSH). Jesus is the
road we must take as believers if we wish to reach the Father’s house. Wiersbe embraces this imagery in terms of
battles we must endure along the way to our home in glory:

      “Who could mind the journey, when the road leads home?” The assurance of a heavenly home at
      the end of life’s road enables us to bear joyfully with the obstacles and battles along the way. It
      was this assurance that even encouraged our Lord, “who for the joy that was set before Him endured
      the cross” (Heb. 12:2). Paul had this truth in mind when he wrote, “For I reckon that the sufferings
      of this present time are not worthy to be compared with the glory which shall be revealed in us”
      (Rom. 8:18).

       If Wiersbe were consistent, he would have to conclude that since entrance into Heaven is not conditioned
on works, something other than entrance into Heaven is envisioned. Unfortunately, he is inconsistent since he says,
“Heaven is the Father’s house.” No, it is not! Not if you must endure trials to reach it! Barclay (NDSB) is more
thorough and much better:

               The Jews talked much about the path or way in which people must walk and the ways of
      God. God said to Moses: ‘You shall not turn to the right or to the left. You must follow exactly the
      path that the Lord your God has commanded you’ (Deuteronomy 5:32–3). Moses said to the people:
      ‘I know that after my death you will surely act corruptly, turning aside from the way that I have
      commanded you’ (Deuteronomy 31:29). Isaiah had said: ‘Your ears shall hear a word behind you,
      saying, “This is the way; walk in it”’ (Isaiah 30:21). In the brave new world, there would be a highway
      called the Way of Holiness, and in it the traveller [sic.], even though a simple soul, would not become
      lost (Is 35:8). It was the psalmist’s prayer: ‘Teach me your way, O Lord’ (Psalm 27:11). The Jews
      knew much about the way of God in which they must walk. And Jesus said: ‘I am the way.’
               What did he mean? Suppose we are in a strange town and ask for directions. Suppose the
      person asked says: ‘Take the first to the right, and the second to the left. Cross the square, go past the
      church, take the third on the right and the road you want is the fourth on the left.’ The chances are that
      we will be lost before we get half-way. But suppose the person we ask says: ‘Come. I’ll take you
      there.’ In that case, the person to us is the way, and we cannot miss it. That is what Jesus does for us.
      He does not only give advice and directions. He takes us by the hand and leads us; he strengthens
      us and guides us personally every day. He does not tell us about the way; he is the way.
               Jesus said: ‘I am the truth.’ The psalmist said: ‘Teach me your way, O Lord, that I may
      walk in your truth’ (Psalm 86:11). ‘For your steadfast love is before my eyes’, he said, ‘and I walk
      in faithfulness to you’ (Psalm 26:3). ‘I have chosen the way of faithfulness,’ he said (Psalm 119:30).
      (Italics his.)

A walk of faithfulness rather than a singular step of faith is conveyed by the imagery of way. Jesus is not
talking about merely entering Him as a gate but of following Him as a way of life. As noted earlier, Barclay
is consistent in that he associates Jn 14:2-3 with rewards:

             (1) The Jews held that in heaven there were different grades of blessedness which would
      be given according to people’s goodness and their fidelity on earth. In the Book of the Secrets of
Misthological Models Part 6                                                                                   Page 174
      Enoch, it is said: ‘In the world to come there are many mansions prepared for men; good for
      good; evil for evil.’ That picture likens heaven to a vast palace in which there are many rooms,
      with each individual assigned a room such as that person’s life has merited.
               (2) In the Greek writer Pausanias, the word monai means stages upon the way. If that is how
      to take it here, it means that there are many stages on the way to heaven, and even in heaven there
      is progress and development and advance. At least some of the great early Christian thinkers had
      that belief. Origen was one. He said that when people died, their souls went to some place called
      Paradise, which is still upon earth. There they received teaching and training and, when they were
      worthy and fit, their souls ascended into the air. They then passed through various monai, stages, which
      the Greeks called spheres and which the Christians called heavens, until finally they reached the
      heavenly kingdom. In so doing, the souls followed Jesus who, as the writer to the Hebrews said,
      ‘passed through the heavens’ (Hebrews 4:14). Irenaeus speaks of a certain interpretation of the
      sentence which tells how the seed that is sown produces sometimes a hundredfold, sometimes sixtyfold
      and sometimes thirtyfold (Matthew 13:8). There was a different yield and therefore a different
      reward. Some people will be counted worthy to pass all their eternity in the very presence of
      God; others will rise to Paradise; and others will become citizens of ‘the city’. Clement of
      Alexandria believed that there were degrees of glory, rewards and stages in proportion to a
      person’s achievement in holiness in this life. (Italics his.)

Barclay’s interpretation is compatible with mine. There are many misthological dwelling places (monai) in 3D New
Jerusalem which are varied in degree of glory according to how well believers perform in their pilgrimage along
their way to the Heavenly City. One may reasonably infer that the same is true in the 4D and 5D chambers of the
Father’s house. The many dwellings owned by faithful believers within these cities will vary in glory in proportion
to believers’ faithfulness and achievements accomplished during their earthly journey to the Heavenly City.
         If Jn 14:2-3 is dealing with rewards, then Jn 14:6 must be also. Conversely, if Jn 14:6 is picturing abiding
in Christ via following His teachings through the power of the Spirit, then Jn 14:2-3 must be dealing with rewards.
On the other hand, if Jn 14:2-3 is simply soteric, then Jn 14:6 must be also. Ironside (AOTG) takes this soteric route
and thus the opposing position:

                Now a word about the Father’s house. Notice it is the Father’s house, and the Father’s house
      is for all the Father’s children. We fear a great many strange things these days. Some people would try
      to tell us that it is only the deeply spiritual people of God that will be caught up with the Lord Jesus at
      His coming. When people talk like that, how little understanding they have of the Father’s heart! Think
      of a normal father and mother here on earth, with say, eight or ten children, and that is quite a family;
      is it not? The father’s house is open to all the children. I pity the home, and pity the children, where
      the father or the mother makes distinctions among their children. I think it is a sad thing when out of
      a number of children one perhaps occupies a special place in the heart of the father and the others are
      held at a distance. “Oh,” but you say, “maybe one or two are naughty children. Of course the father
      could not love naughty children as much as he loves the good children.” Is that true? Why even the
      naughty children are so dear to the father’s heart that they give him many sleepless nights as he thinks
      about their naughtiness. He loves them and truly longs to see them all that they ought to be. There is
      always a welcome for them at the father’s house.
                We need to remember, too, that in the Father’s house above, there is no distinction. People
      often say to me, “Oh, if I can just get into Heaven and get a seat behind the door, I can be satisfied. I
      know I don’t deserve anything better.”
                My dear friend, you don’t deserve to get there at all. I don’t deserve to go there. But I am not
      going there because I deserve to go, but I am going to Heaven because I have been born again and the
      Lord Jesus Christ is preparing a place for me, and the Father’s house is for all the Father’s children.
                Another thing is this: There are no seats behind the door over yonder! I wish everybody would
      realize this. There are no distinctions in the welcome that believers will have in the Father’s house. I
      repeat, the Father’s house has the same welcome for all the Father’s children.
                You say, “Well, but doesn’t the Bible indicate some will have greater rewards than others?”
      Oh, yes, but rewards have nothing to do with the welcome into the Father’s house. The rewards
      specially have to do with the coming glorious kingdom, of course given in Heaven, given at the
Chapter 4. God’s Misthological Temple                                                                          Page 175
         judgment-seat of Christ, but the differences are in the kingdom. For instance, look at the Second Epistle
         of Peter: “So an entrance shall be ministered unto you abundantly into—” Into what? Into Heaven?
         No, it is not true that some people will get an abundant entrance into Heaven and other folk will not
         have anything like so warm and cordial a welcome. What does it mean? It says that some people have
         an entrance ministered unto them abundantly. Yes, but into what? “Into the everlasting kingdom of
         our Lord and Saviour Jesus Christ.” Don’t confuse, don’t confound in your thinking, the Father’s house
         with the everlasting kingdom. The Father’s house is the home of the saints; the everlasting kingdom
         is the sphere of service and rewards, where through all eternity, first in the millennium and then in the
         ages to come, we shall be serving our blessed Lord who has prepared a place for us in the Father’s
         house.

          At the time I wrote TOD, I would have been sympathetic with Ironside’s interpretation. Now, I reject it.
When the kingdom is equated spatially with the realm of God’s rule, thus with Heaven, then we should affirm that
all of God’s children, even the naughty ones, will live with God in His kingdom, that is, in Heaven. Even so, this
does not mean that God’s disobedient children live with God in His house. Brats will not be the Bride. The Father’s
brats will live in their own dwelling places within the kingdom, not in His personal dwelling place. We might picture
it this way: God has a three-storied house in His kingdom, and His children who have lived in harmony with Him
during their time on Earth will live with Him in His house within His kingdom. Those of His children who have not
lived in harmony with Him on Earth will live elsewhere in His kingdom, in houses of their own within the kingdom.
They will live in their Father’s kingdom but not in their Father’s palace.
          Jesus indicates such to be the case when He limits seeing God to those believers who are pure in heart
during their time on Earth (Mt 5:8). The writer of Hebrews makes it clear that seeing God is a reward for a life of
sanctification: “Pursue peace with all men, and the sanctification without which no one will see the Lord”
(Heb 12:14). To be a member of this household, living under the same roof with the Lord, we must be faithful: “But
Christ was faithful as a Son over His house whose house we are, if we hold fast our confidence and the boast of our
hope firm until the end” (Heb 3:6). Living with the Father in His house is what constitutes making you a member
of His household. Seeing the Father’s face as a member of that household is limited to those believers who live in
that house. Consequently, personally seeing the Father’s face is a reward limited to those believers who value
intimacy with the Father presently since only they will share this abode with the Father (Jn 14:23-24). Jesus is
talking about such life as a reward. Exell documents St. Bernard as rightly saying regarding Jn 14:6: “The way, in
which we walk by charity; the truth, to which we cling by faith; the life, to which we aspire by hope. The life in
His example, the truth in His promise, the life in His reward (St. Bernard).”145 By walking in His way, we follow
His life as our way of life and thus attain life as our reward. Excell and Bernard do well.
          Even so, not everyone who affirms that this passage is talking about rewards knows what they are talking
about. Far from it! Consistency is a rarity. To be in harmony with John’s thoughts, one must be able to discern that
(1) entrance into the kingdom is freely given soteriologically to all who believe in Christ alone for eternal life as a
free gift while (2) simultaneously affirming that living in the Father’s house is a superlative misthological dimension
of eternal life given to faithful believers. Most commentators on this passage are muddled in their thinking. For
instance, Eaton (TBEB) takes a soteriological view of Jn 14:2-3, mistakenly giving the impression that “Jesus is
going to do everything that needs to be done to prepare a room for us” so that “He will one day receive us into this
heavenly palace.” Not so. Jesus is preparing this place for those believers who are preparing themselves for this
place. The Bride has a part to play in the preparation: “And it was given to her to clothe herself in fine linen, bright
and clean; for the fine linen is the righteous acts of the saints” (Rev 19:8). Concerning this passage in Revelation,
Eaton does much better, stating:

         The bride gets herself ready by godly living….
         ….Saved people are invited [to the marriage-supper of the Lamb] but they have to get themselves
         ready. I believe that if some of the saved do not get ready, the will be excluded from the marriage-
         supper though they are saved (which seems to be another way of saying what is in 1 Cor 3:15). No
         part of the bride of Christ will presented to him if that part is unclean….all [believers] reach heaven,
         but some of God’s elect will miss sharing in the day of presentation.


145
      Joseph S. Exell, The Biblical Illustrator: St. John, vol. 2 (London: James Nisbet & Co., n.d.), 492.
Misthological Models Part 6                                                                                     Page 176
          In short, all believers will be in Heaven, but only faithful believers will qualify to be a part of the Bride of
Christ and thus attend the marriage-supper in the Heavenly City. The Heavenly City is only a small part of Heaven.
Yet it is the most important part. Participation in that part is conditioned on present sanctification. Returning now
to Jn 14:6, Eaton affirms that Jesus is saying, “I am the way (the pathway to the heavenly glory).” Affirming that
the means is a pathway and the result is heavenly glory is consistent with a misthological understanding. Basically,
Jesus is saying that He is the means by which the Bride may prepare Herself for the marriage-supper. By abiding
in Jesus, via obeying His word through the power of the Holy Spirit, the Bride can become experientially holy in
this life and thus qualify for misthological glory in the next life. Jesus supplies the means for the Bride to prepare
Herself. Indeed, He is the means by which the Bride is to prepare Herself.
          Jesus’ warning regarding the straight and narrow way that leads to life versus destruction in Mt 7:13-14 is
very applicable: “Enter by the narrow gate; for the gate is wide, and the way is broad that leads to destruction, and
many are those who enter by it. For the gate is small, and the way is narrow that leads to life, and few are those who
find it.” Eaton’s comments on this passage are excellent. As Eaton explains, although this passage may have a
secondary application to unbelievers, the primary warning is for believers. Unfaithful believers can suffer a Gehenna
Bema, to use my term, which is an apt term to summarize Dillow’s excellent exposition (Destiny, 878). He dedicates
a chapter to the discussion of Mt 7:13-14 and equates it with Jesus’ exhortation in Lk 9:23 for believers to take up
their cross daily and follow Jesus (p. 294). Eaton affirms that unfaithful believers can have their works burnt up by
the fires of Gehenna/Hell (Mt 5:22; 1Cor 3:15; Rev 2:11). Misthological destruction is entailed. To be consistent,
Eaton and Dillow should switch their interpretation of Jn 14:6, as I have done for my own view, from a soteriological
vantage point to a misthological one.


        Conclusion
        OT and intertestamental material anticipate an eschatological temple built by the Messiah. God’s house is
His temple. Multiple lines of evidence suggest that Jesus was alluding to this temple in Jn 14:2-3 as His Father’s
house. Nevertheless, rather than use oikos for house, which would be the word normally associated with the temple
(cp. LXX and Jn 2:16), Jesus uses oikia in Jn 14:2, which might be used more generically to refer to the Father’s
dwelling as a house, rather than a stereotype temple. My hypothesis is that Jesus used the more comprehensive term
to convey a misthological duality. The first level of meaning—house—suggests New Jerusalem, the 3D City. The
second level of meaning—temple—hints at something added above New Jerusalem, namely the 5D City. New
residencies are being prepared in 3D New Jerusalem for Jesus’ followers. Additionally, an entirely new 5D City is
being prepared for His followers as the upper bridal chamber. In harmony with temple typology, the 5D City is in
an upper dimension to the Father’s present Holy Place.
        These upper realms are inaccessible to lower creatures. Therefore, angels cannot aspire to reach this upper
location. The transcendent nature of this upper realm is implied by Jesus’ Where-I-AM statements. This Where-I-
Am location is one which Jesus shared with the Father and one which He was preparing to share with His faithful
followers. The misthological nature of this place which He is preparing is indicated by multiple texts (cp. Jn 12:26;
13:8; 14:23). The argument can be made that Jn 17:24 adds a soteriological dimension to this location so that it is a
soteric-mistholic duality. However, the more probable interpretation is that Jn 14:2-3 is a mistholic-mistholic, 3D-
5D duality and that Jn 17:24 is exclusively misthological in its realization, probably focused on the higher 5D
misthological aspect of the misthological 3D-5D duality of Jn 14:2-3. The Upper Room Discourse is focused on
misthological concerns, and the Upper Room Prayer is focused on the highest misthological realization that can be
obtained by those believers who faithfully keep God’s word. Only faithful believers will obtain either the 3D or 5D
misthological actualization. Unfaithful believers will be put to shame and sent to the outskirts of the kingdom,
namely the 4D outer darkness.
